Hello observers and imagers of comets,

as maintainer of the image gallery of the German comet section I would
like to invite all comet observers to upload their
images/sketches/videos to the gallery.

Please feel free to upload it http://kometen.fg-vds.de/pix/test/up2_e.php

You can find the images at http://kometen.fg-vds.de/bildere.htm for
the current year or all images available in the gallery at
http://kometen.fg-vds.de/cometlist_e.htm.

If you want to know where the comet observers are located in your
country or in the world use my list or the Google map

http://www.cometchaser.de/observers/names.html
http://www.cometchaser.de/observers/map.html

of my project http://www.cometchaser.de/observers/cometobservers.html

- --

Hi Alfons,

I imaged comet C/2010 G2 as well this evening, and i can confirm the same bright nucleus!
starshape nucleus of 17 arc.sec.and with magnitude increasing (focas Multibox) of 1,5 from my last observation of 28 dec.

Hi All

we perfomed some follow-up of C/2010 G2 (Hill) remotely from the
Faulkes FTS few minutes ago on 2012, January 03.46 through a 2.0-m
f/10.0 Ritchey-Chretien + CCD. The images confim the comet as a bright
star-like object of magnitude about 13.2N

Date:  Thu, 05 Jan 2012 11:17:22 +1030
From:  Andrew 
Subject:  [Comet-Images] comet C/2010 G2 Hill Animation
Hi all,

A small 16 minute animation of Comet C/2010 G2 Hill, taken lastnight
4th-5th January, 2012. Taken with an 80mm f450mm refractor on an Alt Az
mount. 10sec per sub frame, 12 stacked frames per Animation Frame. 8
Frames in the Animation.

http://i363.photobucket.com/albums/oo73/AstromanSID/Astronomy/Comets/comet_hill_001.gif

Quite easily seen now on such short exposures.

Andrew Wall,
South Australia 

Date:  Fri, 06 Jan 2012 11:55:47 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet Lovejoy today - 2012 Jan 5 UT
Hi,

I imaged Comet Lovejoy this morning (2012 January 05.62 UT) after the Moon had set. Used various lenses, etc. Here’s one with a 70-200mm Sigma lens @70mm @f2.8, 500D DSLR @1600 ISO, 5 x 2 minute sublights. FOV = 17 x 12 degrees.
http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_lovejoy-2011w3-500D-70mm_f2,8-5x2min@1600iso-120106_nzdt-john_drummond-web.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/88rorec

and here’s one with a a 20mm Canon lens on the 500D @ f3.2 @ 1600iso, 7 x 1 minute exposures. I THINK I can trace the tail to 35 degrees... Astro twilight had started so had some gradient problems...
http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_lovejoy-2011w3-500D-20mm_f3,2-7x1min@1600iso-120106_nzdt-web.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/724ge2b

I couldn’t see the comet with the naked eye. Dark sky location.

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory Complex
International Astro Union Code: E94
Gisborne, New Zealand
E: 177d 53', S: 38d 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm
Phone (mobile): 0275 609 287
Date:  Thu, 05 Jan 2012 17:16:59 -0600

Date:  Tue, 10 Jan 2012 15:19:54 +1100
From:  Ian Musgrave & Peta O'Donohue 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] image comet C/2010 G2 Hill after outburst.
G'Day All

For those interested, I attempted to measure the intensity of C/2010 G2
Hill using images from the STEREO spacecraft, the comet came into view in
the STEREO H1a instrument on 4 Jan, but was not in such a good position
for attempted astrometry.

My astrometry of C/2010 G2 Hill from 5-Jan to7-Jan yields a magnitude of
12.1 for all days.

It's pretty hard to get decent values as the comet is very close to
brighter stars and right close to the limit of detection (mag 13). I also
can't work out accurately the 95% confidence interval for these values
(but its on the order of +/- 1).

The magnitudes were generated by measuring the intensities of the comet
and nearby reference stars in ImageJ then generating a standard curve from
the reference stars in Graphpad prism, and interpolating the intensity of
the comet from this curve (yes, I know this is rubbish, but it's what I
have to work with). Reference stars are
Star Magnitude
TYC 660-105-1 8.45
TYC 660-293-1 9.81
TYC 660-877-1 10.93
TYC 660-48-1 11.22
TYC 660-579-1 11.8
TYC 660-944-1 12.57

Cheers! Ian

Date:  Sun, 22 Jan 2012 23:30:56 -0000
From:  John 
Subject:  Garradd C2009 P1
Hi,

I woke up at 4:40am just in time to catch Comet Garradd C2009 P1 rising above a tree to the northeast. Visual inspection through my 5" Starfire refractor revealed a slightly greenish diffused glow with a faint star-like nucleus that responded well to higher magnifications. I quickly took a series of 30 second exposures with a new and more sensitive Nikon D7000 at ISO6400 to test its CMOS capable of up to ISO25600. The result is encouraging. Along with a distinct blue-green coma, a faint tail and anti-tail were also captured.

http://stardustobservatory.org/upload/comets/GarraddC2009P1Jan2220122105UTAP127f8D7000ISO64008x30sec-Nassr_20120122232050.jpg

John

From:  denis buczynski 
Subject:  Comet images January26/27/28
Hello all,
Please find below links to comet images taken from Highland Scotland during the past few nights
Best wishes and clear skies
Denis Buczynski,Secretary, Comet Section, British Astronomical Association

49P/Arend-Rigaux

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=439&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=440&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

C/2010S1 LINEAR

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=437&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=438&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

246P/NEAT

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=441&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=442&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

C/2011F1 LINEAR

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=443&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=444&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

I would also like to invite you to follow this link to view our article about the post perihelion
appearance of C2011 W3 Lovejoy

http://britastro.org/journal/pdf/122-1notes.pdf

I would also like to invite you to follow this link to view our article about C/2009P1 Garradd

http://britastro.org/journal/pdf/122-1forum.pdf

Date:  Mon, 30 Jan 2012 15:58:48 +0100
From:  ligustri rolando 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: begins the  approach
> Hi Rolando.
> Another question:
> How can you take 840 sec. of total expose without comet showing movement?
> If you do it afterwards onto processing, how process images with no trace of
> startrails?
> I've tried some times using sigma-clipping but I never achieved a good result.
> Thanks and congrats by you fantastic image!
> Pepe.

For some years i tried to go crazy i also with various programs of elaboration, but
in the end i opted for a trick:

the movement is there, but drowned inside the fake core, so you don't see :-)))

I have seen that up to 5-6 pixels of movement , does not note the error. better, if
you use color ccd, in this case, you can further increase the moved tolerable

Let's take an example :

comet Garradd now moves about 1.7"/min

with this setup:
apo 106/530 ccd STL11000 in bin 2

I can do : RGB=2' each filter and 10-15' with clear
otherwise: RGB=2' each filter in bin 2, and 5' with clear in bin1

with this setup:
apo 106/530 ccd STL8300C

single shot 10-15'

However there is a technique better, it is enough to see the beautiful images of
Michael Jager
But i did not know :-)))

best regards
Rolando

PS: Sorry all, for my terrible english

Date:  Mon, 30 Jan 2012 19:45:20 -0800
From:  andres chapman 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] begins the  approach
My pleasure Ian.About processing comet images I`ve been using Deep Sky Stacker, there you can choose two different type of comet stacking methods.One, the comet is stacked and the stars will appear with trails.The other way you can choose to preserve the comet and stars sharp,best to achieve images like Rolando does.Deep Sky Stacker is a free soft, by the way.I hope you can understand my bad English too..Best wishes, Andres Chapman.

Hi Rolando.

I ended using the same technique as you, but I was more conservative and only allowed 2 pixels of movement. I think could leave more pixels...

About your setup example 10-15' with apo 106/530 & ccd STL8300C, I guess that is using at least bin 2, is correct?

I'm also loving Jager's images!
I studied your images and seem he left 6-7 pixels of movement on shots in L, and afterwards he moves RGB stacked for coincide onto L.

Pepe.

--- In Comet-Images@yahoogroups.com, "ligustri rolando" wrote:
>
> > Hi Rolando.
> > Another question:
> > How can you take 840 sec. of total expose without comet showing movement?
> > If you do it afterwards onto processing, how process images with no trace of
> > startrails?
> > I've tried some times using sigma-clipping but I never achieved a good result.
> > Thanks and congrats by you fantastic image!
> > Pepe.
>
> For some years i tried to go crazy i also with various programs of elaboration, but
> in the end i opted for a trick:
>
> the movement is there, but drowned inside the fake core, so you don't see :-)))
>
> I have seen that up to 5-6 pixels of movement , does not note the error. better, if
> you use color ccd, in this case, you can further increase the moved tolerable
>
> Let's take an example :
>
> comet Garradd now moves about 1.7"/min
>
> with this setup:
> apo 106/530 ccd STL11000 in bin 2
>
> I can do : RGB=2' each filter and 10-15' with clear
> otherwise: RGB=2' each filter in bin 2, and 5' with clear in bin1
>
> with this setup:
> apo 106/530 ccd STL8300C
>
> single shot 10-15'
>
> However there is a technique better, it is enough to see the beautiful images of
> Michael Jager
> But i did not know :-)))
>
> best regards
> Rolando
>
> PS: Sorry all, for my terrible english

Date:  Thu, 23 Feb 2012 17:45:25 +0530
From:  amar sharma 
Subject:  Introduction...and new comet images
Hello comet imagers,

Greetings from India! This is a long time silent member of the comet yahoo groups, but a long time hardcore comet devotee from a place where hardly one or two amateurs follow or have any interest in comets!

I had communicated with couple of you some months ago for buying a CCD camera. I settled with a SBIG ST-8XME self guiding camera in October 2011. I am very happy with it since I've just made my entry into the imaging world as a newbie...with a looong way to go ahead following in your footsteps. Now I cannot believe I am already posting here!

I currently work at a private institute with a C-14 Edge HD, in the southern part of India, off a large city (population: ~15 million!) called Bangalore. We get good part of southern skies being at latitude 12* North.

Our city is the only horrifying one, which suffers among the WORST weather in India, and lowest number of clear skies; from January to March i.e. not more than 90 best clear nights!

However, now on you will see more comet images from me. I am foreseeing venturing into astrometry and photometry from my images. Here are some old shots in my personal but temporary album. These are with a 0.62x Optec focal reducer on the CCD imaging train [the GOTO of the scope is BAD due to imbalance, yet I am managing taking these difficult shots!]:

1) Last month at around the same date:
a) 78/P Gehrels-2
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5699042788954034562
b) 21/P G-Z
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5699039434265451090
c) C/2010 G2 Hill
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5699044182962802802
d) 255/P Levy
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5699044436716552338

2) C/2009 P1 Garradd
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5704105782870820498

3) 49/P H-M-P
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5704105544754606018

4) C/2012 C2 Bruenjes just within days of its discovery
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5709296080575395954

5) 29/P SW-1 in the recent outburst
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5711485945127777794

6) 246/P LINEAR [After seeing an image by Charles Bell on FacceBook, I went for this the same night]
https://picasaweb.google.com/amar10sharma/SBIGST8XMECCDCamera#5712225095734030994

And if anyone of you happens to visit India for any reason, or refer your friend, please stop over with your travel itenerary at Bangalore, at our Observatory. :-)

Do help this newbie grow with your valuable inputs and mentoring. Thanks to all, Amar A. Sharma.

Date:  Sun, 26 Feb 2012 09:38:54 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  c2009 P1 Garrard this morning
This link will take you to the complete comet archives of ASO; Comet 2009 P1 is
currently the first listed observed comet; click on the 2009 P1 Garrard and it will
open the history of this comet and there are TWO entries from this morning:
http://www.arksky.org/php/ctable.php

Mono. and Color image of 2009 P1 Garrard, showing dust tail (right) and ion tail
(left); field is 57 x 75, South is UP

1) Top monochrome, showing both dust and gas tails
and
2) Second entry: RGB under brighter than ideal skies, but showing the color variance
between the dust and ion tails.

Both images are near dawn 09:37 to 09:45 UT and taken with a 110mm f/4.9 APO, ST2000
XM, binned 1x1;

Sorry I could not provide a direct link on this, but the URL keeps getting chopped
when I attempt.

Clay
_____
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
MPC H45 - Petit Jean Mountain South
MPC H41 - Petit Jean Mountain
MPC H43 - Conway West
http://www.arksky.org/

Date:  Tue, 28 Feb 2012 09:52:56 +0100
From:  Gerald Rhemann 
Subject:  comet garradd and disconnection event
Hello everybody,

This is an image of the comet taken in the morning of 21 February. It is the
first time that I have imaged the start of a disconnection in the ion tail
of this comet. It is a two frame mosaic and it was very tricky to process
because the comet is moving rapidly.

http://www.astrostudio.at/2_Bright%20Comets.php?img=images/2_Bright%20Comets
/127_garradd21022012.jpg

I have also uploaded one video where one can see the disconnection on the
very noise stretched single frames:


http://www.astrostudio.at/Videos/JPGVideo1.avi

Images from this week will follow soon.

Regards

Gerald

Subject:  Image of opposite tails of Garradd

Because of it is approaching another time to us, the comet Garradd has increased meaningfully your size and brightness, reaching 6.5 magnitude and becoming
observable at naked eye from very dark sites. Photographically your image shows clearly your both tails, of whitish dust and bluish gas, completely opposite
one direction contrary to other, because of our viewing angle:

http://cometografia.es/2012/02/frente-colas-garradd/

Regards.

José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Sat, 03 Mar 2012 10:48:02 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Comet Garrard_A Tale of Two Tails
Our early morning effort at Comet Garrard at about 09:20 UT after the moon had set;
some high haze and clouds result in faint halos around brighter stars, but both tails
are magnificent, tracing each for over 21 arc minutes.

http://www.arksky.org/asoimg/Com16E50565.jpg

The black and white (monochrome) is a single 150 second image and clearly shows both
the dust (to the right) and Gas/ion (to the left) tail of the comet in great detail;
the ION tail measures to be over 26 arc minutes in length.

The piggyback wide field comet telescope, a 110mm f/4.9 APO refractor riding on the
large observatory astrograph took these images, which cover 47 x 75 arc minutes of
sky, over twice the diameter of the full moon; thus some idea of the size of the
greenish coma, or head, of the comet can be realized. The camera used was the wide
field comet camera, a modified ST2000 XM with color filter wheel computer operated.

The comet is presently in the constellation of DRACO, high in northern skies about
dawn; the comet will continue to brighten and be a spectacular sight until at least
late May of this year. At magnitude 6.6, as measured at the observatory on March 3
the comet is easily seen in binoculars or a small telescope and will appear as a
conspicuous "fuzzy star"; the tails of the comet will not be seen with small
instruments.

Clay
_____
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
MPC H45 - Petit Jean Mountain South
MPC H41 - Petit Jean Mountain
MPC H43 - Conway West
http://www.arksky.org/ 

Date:  Sun, 04 Mar 2012 05:22:42 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  c2009 P1 Garrard March 4
Comet Garrard this morning, with moon setting in west; note the distinct
color/spectral variation between the ion tail (bluish, left) and the dust tail
(reddish, right); the ion tail is quite narrow and long, measured about 23 arc
minutes.

http://www.arksky.org/asoimg/Com16E60BA5.jpg

Image details: Field of view = 75 x 43', south is UP; 110mm f/4.9 APO with ST2000
XM, RGB, no post processing. 180 minutes each, R, G, B; March 04 02:40 UT.

Clay
_____
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
MPC H45 - Petit Jean Mountain South
MPC H41 - Petit Jean Mountain
MPC H43 - Conway West
http://www.arksky.org/

The comet´s ion tail is very active. Thus the structures of the tail are

Let me answer in advance of Alfons Diepvens. With my apologies.

According to the studs measures m2, on the site observers from France, it appears early in the month of March a positive slope that was slightly engaged.

In any case the phenomenon is rather sudden.
Indeed, the 16 March images show no double tail ...

Hello Jean-François, Giovanni,

my CCD brightness of this comet can be found at the following URL

http://www.astronomie.be/alfons.diepvens/cometimages/Lightcurve/49P_Arend-Rigaux.html

The ionstaart can be confirmed by the position angle of the sun at that time.
That is 359° (calculated by Jean Meeus) on the
basis of the comet's position and the position of the sun at that moment!
See Url:
http://www.astronomie.be/alfons.diepvens/cometimages/new/new19.html

But remarkably still fairly bright ion tail!

Date:  Fri, 23 Mar 2012 12:31:48 -0700
From:  Charles Bell 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] NEW images 22 Mar. 2012: Comet 49p
Using JPL Ephemeris output default settings for small bodies on comet 49P:

The position angle, PsAng , of the extended Sun->target radius vector at the
time of these observations was about 177 degrees which should correspond to PA
of ion tail.

You may have some amount of image rotation which an astrometric plate solution
should calculate and record in output log file. In Astrometrica, look
in Astrometrica.log file

Date__(UT)__HR:MN PsAng
2012-Mar-20 00:00 183.167
2012-Mar-21 00:00 180.924
2012-Mar-22 00:00 178.747
2012-Mar-23 00:00 176.636
2012-Mar-24 00:00 174.592
2012-Mar-25 00:00 172.613
2012-Mar-26 00:00 170.699
2012-Mar-27 00:00 168.850
2012-Mar-28 00:00 167.064
2012-Mar-29 00:00 165.339
2012-Mar-30 00:00 163.675
2012-Mar-31 00:00 162.068
2012-Apr-01 00:00 160.518
2012-Apr-02 00:00 159.022

PsAng PsAMV =
The position angles of the extended Sun->target radius vector ("PsAng")
and the negative of the target's heliocentric velocity vector ("PsAMV"),
as seen in the observer's plane-of-sky, measured CCW (east) from reference
frame North Celestial Pole. Small-bodies only. Units: DEGREES.

Date:  Sun, 25 Mar 2012 05:10:13 -0500
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 20120323  comet 49P
I have recorded a trace of this tail, stretching like a fine line due south and then curving rapidly to the west; I have posted a preliminary image on the Comet Archive pages of the ASO website
www.arksky.org
Simply click on the archive link (left column) and then scroll to "49P" and there is a link there. That raw image (negative) does show the faint extension, but I will work up a better image later today.

But the odd tail is real and not an artifact in Alfons' original posting of this odd structure.

This was with the 0.51m astrograph, f/4.9 3 x 120s each, binned 2x2, ST2000 XM

Clay
_____
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod

Date:  Mon, 26 Mar 2012 20:54:27 +0200
From:  Gerald Rhemann 
Subject:  comet Garradd 25 03 2012 last night
Hello everybody,

The last images of comet Garradd from last week suggest the assumption that
the ion tail appears weaker from day to day. Hence I have been surprised to
find a bright ion tail on the images from last night with different
structures which are clearly marked on the single frames (as one can see it
on the video) but are washed out on the stacked final image.

The image:

http://www.astrostudio.at/2_Bright%20Comets.php?img=images/2_Bright%20Comets
/134_garradd25032012.jpg

The video:

www.astrostudio.at/Videos/Garradd25032012

best regards

Gerald

From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] comet Garradd 25 03 2012 last night
To this point, and showing the distinctive dust as well as the ion tail, is an image from March 25 taken under very dark skies at ASO, 180sec x 3 stacked from our wide field f/4.9 110mm APO.
Two photos are on this date, the first from Comet 49P showing the southward linear and skewed tail, the second photo being of 2009 P1

http://www.arksky.org/cgi-bin/asoimglog.pl

Subject:  C/2010 R1 (LINEAR)
This comet was passing close to a bright star so I tried to catch it with my setup (TSAPO65Q 65/420, Atik 314L+, CLS-CCD / Warszawa, Poland).

First run was at 20:20 UT (20 x 2 min), second started at 23:58 (16 x 2 min). 30.04.2012

* http://www.rkastrofoto.appspot.com/site_media/astro/orig/c2010r1-30-04-2012/comet.jpg
* 2-stack animation: http://www.rkastrofoto.appspot.com/site_media/astro/orig/c2010r1-30-04-2012/anim.gif

Few days ago I tried to catch another "dark" comet with a 65 mm APO and it succeeded.

You can find stacked images on my website:
* http://www.rkblog.rk.edu.pl/astro/my_astro_images/show/246pneat-09052012/

I've sent subframes to my friend that made some astrometry measurements and AFAIK already pushed them further.

The galaxy on the left side is NGC4866.

Date:  Fri, 18 May 2012 23:24:47 -0000
From:  lesterbarnes57 
Subject:  18-5-12 C/2011 L4 Panstarrs
Hi all,

this is my first image of this potentially naked eye comet for early 2013. It is 20x3 minute exposures taken with Takahashi 160mm f3.3 Epsilon Astrograph and Astro 40D camera. The two globular clusters M4 and NGC 6144 are also within the FOv. The streaks to the right are reflections from Antares outside the FOV.

http://i638.photobucket.com/albums/uu109/Lester_045/Comets/7b31495b.jpg

Date:  Wed, 23 May 2012 01:48:18 -0000
From:  amar10sharmaa 
Subject:  C/2011 L4 (PANSTARRS) - 19/05/12
Hello folks,

Posting here after a long time. Since there was a thread on comets-ml about C/2011 L4 fading, I attempted to go for it on 19/05/12 @ 21:45 UT.

I was successful in capturing it. Darks subtracted but no flat frame applied. Unfiltered, 10x60 seconds stacked. Instrument - C-14 Edge HD @ f/6.8 with a SBIG ST-8XME.

https://picasaweb.google.com/100263423283309558687/FaintCometsAndSupernovae#5745536452207653026

Thanks, Amar A. Sharma
Nikaya Observatory
off Bangalore, India
https://picasaweb.google.com/nikayaobservatory

Date:  Fri, 22 Jun 2012 05:29:30 +0800
From:  amar sharma 
Subject:  C/2011 L4 (PANSTARRS): 19-06
Hello comet-eers,

Here is my recent attempt at C/2011 L4, from not clear skies. Conditions in my city are atrocious for a prolonged time - haze, clouds and altitude fog. I have been spending tens and tens of hours under clouds during the past 3 months new moon period.

Sincerely awaiting to get some other comets in this month's list. I aimed the scope at twilight at 96/P however it was very foggy/cloudy at the horizon at day-break. Now 96/P being just 2-3 degree above horizon disappears down each day.
Here is PANSTARRS. There is considerable improvement since I last shot it coincidentally one month ago on the same date:

https://picasaweb.google.com/100263423283309558687/FaintCometsAndSupernovae#5756433726327633506
or

http://tinyurl.com/7gsn4mq
Details:

C-14 EHD @ f/6.8
SBIG ST-8XME
CCD temp negative 2*C
8x60 seconds
No binning
Unfiltered imageDark frames appliedSingle flat frame applied to each light frame

Thanks,

----------Amar A. SharmaNikaya Observatoryoff Bangalore, India+12* 36' / 77E 43'

Date:  Mon, 23 Jul 2012 08:50:31 +0200
From:  Juan José González Suárez 
Subject:  96P/Machholz.
Splendid work, Michael. Many thanks for sharing.

I made a visual estimate of the comet about one houre after your image:

96P/Machholz:
2012 July 22.88 UT: m1=7.8, Dia.=1.5', DC=5,
Tail: 0.1 deg. in PA 60 deg, 20 cm SCT (77x).
[ Altitude: 9 deg. Mountain location, very clear sky.
End of nautical twilight. Comparison stars at the same
low altitude as the comet. Nearby stars down to10.5
magnitude were visible.].

( Alto del Castro - Aralla, alt. 1720 m., Leon, N. Spain ).

Best regards and clear skies,

J. J. Gonzalez

From:  Martin Gembec 
Subject:  96P/Machholz
We saw comet Machholz today evening rather clear through 305/1500 dobsonian. My friend have got blinking sighting also in 125mm binoculars. I tried to image comet with my ED80/600 with Vixen 0.67x reducer. I was surprised with visually observation today, when a week ago it was near Sun. Nice comet, even not so bright.

Images, info and atmosphere of observation on
http://udalosti.astronomy.cz/?p=1526

Martin Gembec

Date:  Sun, 29 Jul 2012 05:35:28 -0700
From:  Charles Bell 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 96P Machholz 1   july 27
To Michael Jäger

This image and fountain like detail in the head/coma are fascinating. Ion tail,
thin, linear. Broad dust tail. The comet has excellent perspective.

The comet's sun-object-earth phase angle is almost 90 degrees giving us an
excellent side view.

Would like to know if this is R filtered monochrome? or V or B or unfiltered
Perhaps B, V, R filtered images would appear slightly different with regard to
coma, dust and ion tail

Thank you. This is a most excellent image.Congratulations on your capture.

Best wishes,

Charles Bell
at H47 Vicksburg

Hi,

the archive of images from the German Fachgruppe Kometen has reached a
new milestone.

Today I added new images to the gallery, crossing the the line of 6000
pictures with having more than 500 comet apparitions in the archive.

You can browse the images at http://kometen.fg-vds.de/bildere.htm

Looking forward to your comments.

I will also invite every comet photographer to upload your images to
the archive at http://kometen.fg-vds.de/pix/test/up2_e.php

Old images are welcomed too.

J95 on September 02.01 on the BAA Gallery at the following link:

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=571&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

link:

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=569&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

Denis Buczynski

Date:  Fri, 07 Sep 2012 07:36:31 +0100
From:  Μanos Kardasis 
Subject:  Comet 2001F1 from Skinakas 1.29m telescope
 Skinakas observatory was built years ago in my motherland Crete:
http://skinakas.physics.uoc.gr/en/
 The use of such a telescope was just a dream for me which just came true.
We had the chance to test planetary and cometary imaging through the 1.29 telescope in
 four consecutive nights 28-31 August.After preparation and a long travel
 we managed to make some observations of Jupiter,Uranus and Neptune and some Comets with G.Maravelias.

Here is our first try on C2011F1:

http://www.astrovox.gr/forum/album_pic.php?pic_id=15568

We were very unlucky on all nights because the seeing was awful so planetary imaging was quite unsuccesful.

http://kardasis.weebly.com/jupiter-2012-13.html

The weather was clear the 3/4 nights but we had strong winds from 5B to 10B!The temperature was around 10deg. and widchil was -4 to 5 deg. C !
here you may find some wide field images from my stay there (the first 6):

http://kardasis.weebly.com/wf-astrophotos.html

 Thanks to T.Kougentakis and G.Maravelias for the cooperation.

More will follow.

 Manos Kardasis

Hi all,

I have uploaded a ccd image of C/2011 L4 PANSTARRS onto my website:

http://members.westnet.com.au/mmatti/sc.htm

2012 Sep 9.4UT.

plus digital development filter to reveal tail curvature in the head of the
comet.

Date:  Wed, 12 Sep 2012 15:00:44 -0000
From:  watchingthesky2003 
Subject:  Re: 168P Hergenrother  LRGB image sep. 10
Very nice image! Just found out about this comet yesterday. Took a remote image out of Spain showing it near the galaxy NGC 186 of the NGC 194 galaxy group. http://www.flickr.com/photos/watchingthesky/7978882473

Viewed it last night with my 17.5-inch Dobsonian at 182x. It had moved a bit north since the above image, but the comet and NGC 186 could fit in the field. The comet was slightly brighter than NGC 186 and appeared fan or funnel shaped. It was about the same size as the galaxy. Viewed the galaxy group while I was at it. I'd say the comet was not quite as bright as the brightest galaxies of the group.

Stan Howerton

Date:  Mon, 08 Oct 2012 22:50:08 +0200
From:  Luc ARNOLD 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 2012-10-05 160P/LINEAR  Fragment(s) ?
Dear all,

Wind and bad seeing yesterday evening, but I managed to get an image of
160P with the 80cm OHP telescope.
The comet shows a faint tail about 100'' long in PA=210, but no trace
of fragment or 'accident' in the tail. Probably noise + a hint of tail
signal are responsible
for the 'blob' detected in the Oct. 5th images...
http://www.obs-hp.fr/~larnold/v2/LucArnold/160P_LINEAR.html

All the best
Luc

Date:  Fri, 12 Oct 2012 22:33:21 -0000
From:  dennis_persyk 
Subject:  Comet 168P images   Cooled CCD and DSLR
DSLR:
Canon T1i
ISO 1600
EF 75 - 300 mm lens at f/5.6
39 x 31 seconds -- limited to only 31 seconds due to flexure in the front-heavy lens and tripod mount

Cooled CCD:
SBIG STF-3800M binned 2x2
TeleVue NP-101 4-inch refractor f/5.4
23 x 2 minutes -- limited by comet relative motion of 1.8 arc seconds/minute and 5 arc second/pixel image scale

Mount: Astro-Physics AP-1200GTO

I was disappointed in the comet magnitude of only 10.8 . A couple of weeks ago it was 8.0 during a brief outburst. That's what I get for waiting.

Please take a look at the web page -- images, isophotes, orbit diagram, light curve -- all kinds of data.

http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm .

Clear skies,

Dennis Persyk
Hampshire, IL
Igloo (Now Roll-Off) Observatory Home Page http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk
New Images http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm
Pier Design http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/Pier_Design.htm
Daily Bread Inspirational Page (Helicopter Parable) http://users.foxvalley.net/~dpersyk/DailyBread/

don't know....

Date:  Sun, 21 Oct 2012 01:27:17 +0200
From:  Gianluca Masi 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 168P: false nucleus
I don't think so.

The appearance of the comet is completely independent from the pattern of the
star trails. Even images with regular star trails show that appearance.

Tonight, the comet is looking as in the attached image. It is one of a couple of
dozen, taken a while ago with the very same system and same parameters as the
previous night (all the images of 168P I took over the previous days shared the
identical choices).

http://www.virtualtelescope.eu/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2012/10/168p_20oct2012.jpg

Best,
Gian

From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 168P: false nucleus
As I process a couple of images of 168P from Oct 18 and Oct 20 I believe that
the elongation of the nucleus is real and not an artifact, not of guiding nor
tracking. The nucleus under high resolution is clearly elongated in short (i.e.
40 second) images from our files, this elongation not in line with the actual
apparent motion of the comet.

What is reported as a "false nucleus" is a definite elongation of the central
condensation and there is indeed a slight "hint" of separation on both images
from these dates.
I will get these posted later tonight.

Dr. Clay
_____
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
MPC H45 - Petit Jean Mountain South
MPC H41 - Petit Jean Mountain
MPC H43 - Conway West
http://www.arksky.org/

From:  "P. Clay Sherrod"

Now posted on the Arkansas Sky Observatories webpage:
http://www.arksky.org/smf/index.php/topic,2065.0.html

two quickly prepared (no additional processing, just raw images) images of 168P
from Oct. 18 and 20 (UT).
These two images do indeed suggest some type of secondary fragmentation in the
direction of the tail of the comet away from the nucleus OR some severe
elongation of the nucleus in that direction (nearly Southeast from the main
comet center).

Click on each image to enlarge for view.

By an incredible cosmic coincidence one of the SLOOH telescopes-for-rent
was pointed at 168P about 15 minutes ago during an 11-hour marathon
streamed for free at http://events.slooh.com - see
http://twitpic.com/b5ziig for a screenshot of a color image. I have no
clue about the optical parameters of the telescope used and what a
'normal' comet of this brightness would look, but the inner coma looks
pretty elongated to me. The same was true for a b/w image shown just
before this one.

Date:  Sun, 21 Oct 2012 02:54:59 -0000
From:  chergen 
Subject:  Re: 168P: false nucleus


I can confirm Gianluca's and Clay's observations of 168P.
Observations with the Univ. of Arizona's Kuiper 1.54-m
show a "cloud" of material trailing the nucleus in the
anti-solar direction.

My images can be seen at:

http://transientsky.wordpress.com/2012/10/20/comet-hergenrother-in-outburst/

The comet looks very similar in appearance to comet
73P-B/Schwassmann-Wachmann 3 when it was shedding material
during its outbursts in 2006. As HST and Subaru showed,
73P-B's "clouds" were composed of hundreds to thousands
of small mini-comets caused by small boulders. It is
possible that 168P is experiencing something similar as
these boulders slowly drift away from the main nucleus
while continuing to release dust and gas on their own. You
can see how 73P-B's "clouds" played out at:

http://www.lpl.arizona.edu/~chergen/73PB.html

Whatever we call this, it seems to lie somewhere between a
typical outburst and a splitting event. Then again maybe
most large outbursts produce similar "clouds" that we are
now only recognizing due to the large number of CCD imagers.

- Carl

Date:  Sun, 21 Oct 2012 08:58:00 -0500
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  ASO comparison image of 168P from Oct 212
I have posted on the ASO comet digest pages a dual image from October 21 (UT) of
comet 168P, showing the overall structure of the comet (top positive image)
along with a higher resolution negative image adjusted for reduced density to
examine the nucleus of the comet. This is a follow-up of the reported possible
fragmentation or outgassing of the primary nucleus earlier this week.

http://www.arksky.org/php/cdata_admin.php?object=168PxxxHergenrother

Although the elongation of Oct. 18 and 20 of the nucleus (fragmentation?) is
still evident, there is not so much of a clear definition of what might be
called a "false" or dislocated fragment of the nucleus.
Compare this view with those posted yesterday from ASO at:
http://www.arksky.org/smf/index.php/topic,2065.0.html

Both images are 45 sec. each with the 0.51m DK astrograph from Arkansas Sky
Observatories, with north up and field about 25 x `12 ' arc.

Dr. Clay

Date:  Wed, 24 Oct 2012 09:54:45 -0500
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  ASO update on 168P_Secondary nucleus measured
Very interesting night with comet 168P (Hergenrother).
The secondary/fragmentation nature of this comet's nucleus could actually be
measured on three exposures (15sec) last night (Oct 24 UT) with the 0.512m DK
astrograph at Arkansas Sky Observatory. Keeping the density and saturation of
the images low allowed for us to see more of the nature of this activity, which
now does suggest an actual splitting or development of secondary mass to the SE
of the main nucleus. For the first time the astrometric program automatically
locked onto the secondary centroid without question.

Measurements are below. A photo from 07:12 this morning UT is posted at:
http://www.arksky.org/php/ctable.php
Find 168P near the top of the Comet Table and click on that link and then find
the image on the posting for Oct. 24.

The information reveals that the secondary nucleus is located 20" away from the
primary component in PA 138.5 deg. This is very close to the tail angle
measured from the same images which is 139 degrees. The magnitude (m2) of this
component was measured at 15.2.

Clay
_____
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
MPC H45 - Petit Jean Mountain South
MPC H41 - Petit Jean Mountain
MPC H43 - Conway West
http://www.arksky.org/

Date:  Wed, 24 Oct 2012 19:16:33 +0100
From:  denis buczynski 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] ASO update on 168P_Secondary nucleus measured
Hello all,
I too have been following and imaging this comet during its recent outburst.I have been closely watching for evidence of secondary fragments near the head of the comet. I have noticed that there are many stars and small galaxies occulted by the head of this comet during its swift passage through these bright starfields. These can sometime look like secondary fragments if images are only obtained over a very short time period. One such occultation occurred last night whilst I imaged the comet. The effect is to be seen in the sequence of images I took last night (at Tarbatness Observatory IAU Code i81) on 20121023 between 22:38 and 23:07 UT. The link to these images is at:

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=640&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

Denis Buczynski
Secretary Comet Section
British Astronomical Association

From: P. Clay Sherrod
Sent: Wednesday, October 24, 2012 3:54 PM
To: comets-ml@yahoogroups.com
Cc: Comet-Images@yahoogroups.com
Subject: [Comet-Images] ASO update on 168P_Secondary nucleus measured

Very interesting night with comet 168P (Hergenrother).
The secondary/fragmentation nature of this comet's nucleus could actually be
measured on three exposures (15sec) last night (Oct 24 UT) with the 0.512m DK
astrograph at Arkansas Sky Observatory. Keeping the density and saturation of
the images low allowed for us to see more of the nature of this activity, which
now does suggest an actual splitting or development of secondary mass to the SE
of the main nucleus. For the first time the astrometric program automatically
locked onto the secondary centroid without question.

Measurements are below. A photo from 07:12 this morning UT is posted at:
http://www.arksky.org/php/ctable.php
Find 168P near the top of the Comet Table and click on that link and then find
the image on the posting for Oct. 24.

The information reveals that the secondary nucleus is located 20" away from the
primary component in PA 138.5 deg. This is very close to the tail angle
measured from the same images which is 139 degrees. The magnitude (m2) of this
component was measured at 15.2.

Clay
_____
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
MPC H45 - Petit Jean Mountain South
MPC H41 - Petit Jean Mountain
MPC H43 - Conway West
http://www.arksky.org/

Date:  Fri, 02 Nov 2012 12:16:28 -0000
From:  denis buczynski 
Subject:  168p Hergenrother
Hello all,
I was also able to image this comet last night, in a dark sky (first with moon out of sky for some
time) and took a set of 20x30s in r band filter to see if the reported fragmentation was visible yet
at 2"/pixel resolution I use with my C14/ST9XE combination. I could not detect any fragment with the
processing I used (stacking and log stretch). I wonder if a drift rate can be calculated from the
fragment from the large telescope images which would give us an indication when it should be
possible for observers using the size of telescope we employ to image the main fragment? I will
continue to image this active comet. I have placed all the images submitted to the BAA Comet
Section on
the Comet Gallery on the BAA Website at:
http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=category&catid=5&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

Direct links to the images I took last night are at:

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=646&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=645&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

An image taken by Nick James a few hours later is also placed on the BAA Comet page at:

http://britastro.org/baa/index.php?view=detail&id=647&option=com_joomgallery&Itemid=200

Date:  Mon, 12 Nov 2012 03:37:03 -0000
From:  alan 
Subject:  168P and cosmic or meteor
At my blog is a recent(2012111-194859) view of Comet 168P via Itelescope T5, using a R-filter and 45sec frames. I am not sure what the little flash is about. It is part of the raw image data, and still visible in calibrated images on the right hand side. I don't think it is part of the comet. Could be a cosmic hit on the sensor or perhaps a micro meteor burst?

A rough avi is at my blog, video compression has distorted it a bit, a small something travels down from just behind comet tail and ends at the splooch....

http://cometal-comets.blogspot.com.au/2012/11/comet-168p-via-itelescopt-t5.html

Any opinions welcome?

Kind regards, Alan Watson

During this last week (BAA member and winner of the 2011 Astronomy Picture of the Year Award) Damian
Peach has been imaging the two brightest comets in the night sky. His images taken with the 50cm CDK
telescope at Mayhill in New Mexico have been placed on the BAA Comet Gallery at the links below.
Denis Buczynski

Date:  Wed, 26 Dec 2012 23:22:25 +0100
From:  Gerald Rhemann 
Subject:  Christmas Comet :_)
Hello everybody,

I hope you enjoyed the holidays.

My last image for this year was taken in the morning of the 24th December.
Comet 2012K5 LINEAR was very near at the bright star Dubhe in Ursa Major.
Thus some reflection streamers caused by this star are visible between
comet and Galaxy NGC 3359:

http://www.astrostudio.at/3_Faint%20Comets.php?img=images/3_Faint%20Comets/0
35_2012K5.jpg

By this way I wish you a Happy New Year

Gerald
